Nucleic Acids Res. 40, e49–e49 (2012)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2012">32</a></sup> was performed using the tomato and potato reference proteins and set of predicted proteins derived from the <i>N. tabacum</i> TN90 RNA-seq data (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms4833#MOESM342">Supplementary Data 8 and 9</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Estimation of the quality of the assembly</h3><p><i>N. tabacum</i> Hicks Broadleaf BAC sequences were sequenced by Roche 454 and assembled with newbler. In total 1,864,003 bases were obtained in sequences longer than 80 kb. The TN90, K326 and BX assemblies were mapped to these BACs sequences using blastn and a threshold of 98% identity, and the identified scaffolds remapped to the BAC sequences using LAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Frith, M. C., Hamada, M. &amp; Horton, P. Parameters for accurate genome alignment. BMC Bioinformatics 11, 80 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2034">57</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Kiełbasa, S. M., Wan, R., Sato, K., Horton, P. &amp; Frith, M. C. Adaptive seeds tame genomic sequence comparison. Genome Res. 21, 487–493 (2011)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2037">58</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Repeat content estimation</h3><p>The repeat content of the genome assemblies was estimated using RepeatMasker with the eudicot repeat library available from the Sol Genomics Network, the TIGR Solanaceae repeat library and RepeatScout<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Price, A. L., Jones, N. C. &amp; Pevzner, P. A. De novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics 21, i351–i358 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2049">59</a></sup> libraries created using sequences of at least 200 kb from the draft genome assemblies. Classification of the repeat types was performed using blastn<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Altschul, S. F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E. W. &amp; Lipman, D. J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403–410 (1990)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2053">60</a></sup> hits to known repeat elements.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Transcriptome assembly and quantitative analysis</h3><p>The transcriptomes were derived by mapping RNA-Seq reads from each variety to the corresponding reference genome. For each variety, three biological replicates were obtained for each tissue. Mapping was performed using the ‘tuxedo’ suite of short read mapping tools (Bowtie v2.0.0 beta<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Fast gapped-read alignment with Bowtie 2. Nat. Methods 9, 357–359 (2012)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2065">61</a></sup>, Tophat v2.0.4 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Kim, D. et al. TopHat2: accurate alignment of transcriptomes in the presence of insertions, deletions and gene fusions. Genome Biol. 14, R36 (2013)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2068">62</a>) and Cufflinks v2.0.2 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Transcript assembly and quantification by RNA-Seq reveals unannotated transcripts and isoform switching during cell differentiation. Nat. Biotechnol. 28, 511–515 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2071">63</a>). The resulting fragments were used as input for the Trinity software suite<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644–652 (2011)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2075">64</a></sup> open reading frame finder; the resulting predicted protein sequences were filtered for uniqueness and used for further analysis. GO terms were assigned to the unique subset of predicted protein sequences using InterProScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Zdobnov, E. M. &amp; Apweiler, R. InterProScan–an integration platform for the signature-recognition methods in InterPro. Bioinformatics 17, 847–848 (2001)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2079">38</a></sup>. Protein clusters were determined using OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178–2189 (2003)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2084">65</a></sup> with standard parameters. Besides the predicted proteins from the TN90 transcriptome, we used the following sources to obtain proteins from other species: SGN for <i>N. benthamiana</i>, ITAG (version 2.3) for <i>S. lycopersicum</i> and TAIR (version 10) for <i>A. thaliana</i>. All protein sets were filtered for a minimum protein size of 100 amino-acid residues.</p><p>For the quantitative analysis, the mapped RNA-seq reads were counted using HTSeq, and DESeq<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Anders, S. &amp; Huber, W. Differential expression analysis for sequence count data. Genome Biol. 11, R106 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2100">66</a></sup> was used to calculate differences in expression between the two tissues. Genes with a 10-fold upregulation and an associated adjusted <i>P</i>-value cutoff of 0.001 were deemed to be significantly differentially regulated. The set of overexpressed genes in leaves and roots was analysed for GO term enrichment. The software tool BiNGO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Maere, S., Heymans, K. &amp; Kuiper, M. BiNGO: a Cytoscape plugin to assess overrepresentation of gene ontology categories in biological networks. Bioinformatics 21, 3448–3449 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2107">67</a></sup> was used to calculate and visualize the enrichment. For determining enriched terms, the hypergeometric test was used with subsequent Benjamini and Hochberg false discovery rate corrections; a <i>P</i>-value threshold of 0.001 was used as a cutoff for inferring enrichment.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Pathway gene identification</h3><p>Genes of interest were identified by mapping TAIR10 or UniProt proteins using BLAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Kent, W. J. BLAT—the BLAST-like alignment tool. Genome Res. 12, 656–664 (2002)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2122">29</a></sup> to the genomes of <i>N. tabacum</i> ancestors <i>N. sylvestris</i> and <i>N. tomentosiformis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Sierro, N. et al. Reference genomes and transcriptomes of Nicotiana sylvestris and Nicotiana tomentosiformis. Genome. Biol. 14, R60 (2013)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2134">15</a></sup>, extracting the identified genomic regions and 5 kb flanking regions, remapping the query protein using Exonerate<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Slater, G. S. C. &amp; Birney, E. Automated generation of heuristics for biological sequence comparison. BMC Bioinformatics 6, 31 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2138">68</a></sup> and predicting the target gene using SNAP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Korf, I. Gene finding in novel genomes. BMC Bioinformatics 5, 59 (2004)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2143">69</a></sup> with the Exonerate hints. The thus-predicted <i>N. sylvestris</i> and <i>N. tomentosiformis</i> coding DNA sequences were then mapped to <i>N. tabacum</i> assemblies, and the <i>N. tabacum</i> coding DNA sequences and proteins were extracted using the above method.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">PCR <i>eIF4</i> gene family detection</h3><p>Sequences related to <i>eIF4E</i> were identified by mapping tomato homologues as described above. In addition to the previously described PVY test primers<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Julio, E., Verrier, J. &amp; de Borne, F. D. Development of SCAR markers linked to three disease resistances based on AFLP within Nicotiana tabacum L. Theor. Appl. Genet. 112, 335–346 (2006)." href="/articles/ncomms4833#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d39418e2174">70</a></sup>, specific primer pairs were designed for each <i>eIF4E</i> member (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms4833#MOESM342">Supplementary Table 13</a>). Genomic DNA of different varieties was isolated as described in the plant section. PCR of genomic DNA was conducted using a 2-ng μl<sup>−1</sup> template, 0.25 μM of each primer and GoTaq Hot Start polymerase (Promega AG, Switzerland). PCR was performed at 95 °C for 8 min, then 40 cycles of 30 s at 95 °C, 55 °C and 72 °C, sequentially, with a final extension at 5 min at 72 °C. PCR products were separated on a 1.2% agarose gel in 0.5 × TAE and visualized using ethidium bromide.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec20" data-title="Additional information"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec20-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec20">Additional information</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec20-content"><p><b>Accession codes:</b> Genome sequence data for <i>Nicotiana tabacum</i> TN90 has been deposited in DDBJ/EMBL/GenBank nucleotide core database under the accession code AYMY00000000. Genome and transcriptome sequencing data for <i>N. tabacum</i> TN90 have been deposited in GenBank Sequence Read Archive (SRA) under the accession code <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRP029183">SRP029183</a>. Genome sequence data for <i>Nicotiana tabacum</i> K326 has been deposited in DDBJ/EMBL/GenBank nucleotide core database under the accession code AWOJ00000000. Genome and transcriptome sequencing data for <i>N. tabacum</i> K326 have been deposited in GenBank Sequence Read Archive (SRA) under the accession code <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRP029184">SRP029184</a>. Genome sequence data for <i>Nicotiana tabacum</i> Basma Xanthi has been deposited in DDBJ/EMBL/GenBank nucleotide core database under the accession code AWOK01000000. Genome and transcriptome sequencing data for <i>N. tabacum</i> Basma Xanthi have been deposited in GenBank Sequence Read Archive (SRA) under the accession code SRP029185. Genome sequence data for <i>Nicotiana otophora</i> has been deposited in DDBJ/EMBL/GenBank nucleotide core database under the accession code AWOL00000000. Genome sequence data for <i>N. otophora</i> have been deposited in GenBank Sequence Read Archive (SRA) under the accession code <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRP028836">SRP028836</a>.</p><p><b>How to cite this article:</b> Sierro, N. <i>et al.</i> The tobacco genome sequence and its comparison with those of tomato and potato. <i>Nat. Commun.</i> 5:3833 doi: 10.1038/ncomms4833 (2014).</p></div></div></section>

N.B. and S.G. contributed to the disease resistance section. S.O. prepared the libraries and performed Illumina sequencing. N.S. and J.N.D.B. carried out genome and transcriptome analysis. N.S., J..N.D.B., L.B., S.G. and N.V.I. wrote the manuscript. N.V.I. supervised the study.
